<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/templates/jsp/pb2/js/plugin/thiss-ds.js" nonce="59456d885555415f8f39f255bb31df16"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="59456d885555415f8f39f255bb31df16">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: '73a047df-f471-4f5b-87ce-5827d249ea4a'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

        (function() {
            function riskifiedBeaconLoad() {

                var session_id = '35D2477EB68FC061F54F25E9C0DC321C';

                s.async = true;
                s.src = url;
                var x = document.getElementsByTagName('script')[0];
                x.parentNode.insertBefore(s, x);
            }

                window.attachEvent('onload', riskifiedBeaconLoad)
            else

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d17171655" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>It is of fundamental and technological significance to develop dual-role anode materials for both lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) with high performance. Here, a composite material based on CoSe<sub>2</sub> nanoparticles encapsulated in N-doped carbon framework intertwined with carbon nanotubes (CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs) is prepared successfully from cobalt-based zeolitic imidazolate framework (ZIF-67). As anode materials for LIBs, CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs composites deliver a reversible capacity of 428 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> even after 500 cycles at a current density of 1 A g<sup>−1</sup> with almost 100% Coulombic efficiency. The charge and discharge mechanisms of CoSe<sub>2</sub> are characterized using ex situ X-ray diffraction and Raman analysis, from which the lithiation products of CoSe<sub>2</sub> are found to be Li<i><sub>x</sub></i>CoSe<sub>2</sub> and Li<sub>2</sub>Se, which are further converted to CoSe<sub>2</sub> upon delithiation. The CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs composites also demonstrate excellent electrochemical performance as anode materials for SIBs with a carbonate-based electrolyte, with specific capacities of 606 and 501 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1 and 1 A g<sup>−1</sup> in the 100th cycle. The electrochemical performance of the anode materials is further studied by pseudocapacitance and galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) measurements. This work may be exploited for the rational design and development of dual-role anode materials for both Li- and Na-ion batteries.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="advs832-sec-0010">
         
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="advs832-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>Recently, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have been attracting significant interests of the scientific communities, because SIBs are believed to be a viable alternative for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), especially in the field of large-scale energy storage.<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0001_R_d17171647e482" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Chem. Rev. Chem. Soc. Rev. Adv. Funct. Mater. ACS Nano Nano Energy">1</a></span> Notably, the redox potential of sodium is only 0.3 V higher than that of lithium, and sodium is of high natural abundance and low costs. However, as the ionic radius of Na is larger than that of Li (0.102 vs 0.076 nm), the electrode host materials that are good for LIBs are not suitable for SIBs.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0001_R_d17171647e484" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Chem. Rev. Chem. Soc. Rev. Adv. Funct. Mater. ACS Nano Nano Energy">1</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0002_R_d17171647e484" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Small Chem. Eng. J. Adv. Energy Mater.">2</a></span>] Yet, it is generally believed that the electrode materials for LIBs and SIBs are relevant to each other and it is highly desired to design electrode host materials that may be used for both LIBs and SIBs.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0001_R_d17171647e487" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Chem. Rev. Chem. Soc. Rev. Adv. Funct. Mater. ACS Nano Nano Energy">1</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0003_R_d17171647e487" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - ACS Energy Lett. Chem. Eng. J.">3</a></span>]</p>
         
         <p>Composite nanomaterials based on transition-metal selenides encapsulated in carbonaceous materials, especially those derived from metal–organic frameworks (MOFs), have demonstrated great promise as dual-role anode materials for both LIBs and SIBs,<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0004_R_d17171647e493" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Nano Energy">4</a></span> primarily due to the high electric conductivity and theoretical capacity.<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0005_R_d17171647e495" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Adv. Mater. Adv. Energy Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Coord. Chem. Rev.">5</a></span> With the unique architecture of the carbon matrix, not only can the transport kinetics of ions and electrons be accelerated, but also the structural collapse resulting from volume changes can be significantly alleviated, thus leading to enhanced insertion/extraction reversibility and improved Li<sup>+</sup>/Na<sup>+</sup> storage capacity.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0003_R_d17171647e501" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - ACS Energy Lett. Chem. Eng. J.">3</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0006_R_d17171647e501" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Energy Environ. Sci. Adv. Funct. Mater. ACS Nano Adv. Energy Mater.">6</a></span>] For example, MoSe<sub>2</sub> nanosheets supported by porous hollow carbon spheres have been prepared by a three-step method and delivered a capacity of 681 and 580 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> for LIBs and SIBs, respectively, after 100 cycles.<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0007_R_d17171647e509" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Nanoscale">7</a></span> CoSe@porous carbon polyhedra (PCP) composites, prepared through the carbonization treatment of cobalt-based zeolitic imidazolate framework (ZIF-67) and further selenization at 650 °C in a N<sub>2</sub> atmosphere, delivered a capacity of 675 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles at a current rate of 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup> for LIBs and 341 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup> for SIBs.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0003_R_d17171647e522" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - ACS Energy Lett. Chem. Eng. J.">3</a></span>]</p>
         
         <p>CoSe<sub>2</sub>/C composites have been prepared in different conditions and demonstrated excellent electrochemical performance as anode materials for SIBs. For example, the application of a H<sub>2</sub>/Ar atmosphere during carbonization of ZIF-67 at 550 °C resulted in the formation of a N-doped carbon framework intertwined with carbon nanotubes.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0002_R_d17171647e532" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Small Chem. Eng. J. Adv. Energy Mater.">2</a></span>] Both orthorhombic and cubic CoSe<sub>2</sub> were observed in X-ray diffraction (XRD) measurements. As anode materials for Na-storage, they displayed a capacity of 424 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles at a current rate of 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup> and 300.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 400 cycles at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>. In another study, Qiu and co-workers<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0008_R_d17171647e546" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - J. Mater. Chem. A﻿﻿">8</a></span> carbonized ZIF-67 in H<sub>2</sub>/Ar at 600 °C to form a carbon matrix embedded with Co nanoparticles bridged by carbon nanotubes (Co@C/CNTs). Vaporizing Se powder at 360 °C and further reaction of Se vapor with Co nanoparticles imbedded inside the carbon matrix for 10 h resulted in the formation of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@C/CNTs composite. When served as the anodes for SIBs, CoSe<sub>2</sub>@C/CNTs exhibited a stable cycling performance with a reversible capacity of 390 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> over 1000 cycles at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>. Although such CoSe<sub>2</sub>/C composites demonstrated excellent cycling stability as anode materials for SIBs, the gas–solid flow reaction requires continuous input of high energy and is not suitable for large-scale industrial production. Most importantly, the investigation of CoSe<sub>2</sub> as dual anode materials for both LIBs and SIBs, their charge and discharge mechanisms, as well as the electrolyte effect on the battery performance have remained largely unexplored.</p>
         
         <p>Inspired by the abovementioned structural modification strategies, in this work, CoSe<sub>2</sub> nanoparticles encapsulated into a N-doped carbon framework that was intertwined with carbon nanotubes (CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs) was synthesized successfully by a facile MOF-engaged approach, which is suitable for mass production in industry. The derived CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs composite materials demonstrated superior electrochemical performance as anode materials for both LIBs and SIBs.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="advs832-sec-0020">
         
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="advs832-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="advs832-sec-0030">
            
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="advs832-sec-0030-title">2.1 Structural Analysis</h3>
            
            <p>The scanning electron microscopy (SEM) images of the prepared polyhedral ZIF-67 template were shown in Figure S1 (Supporting Information), which showed a smooth surface. From <b>Figure</b> <a href="#advs832-fig-0001">1</a>a, after pyrolysis under a reductive Ar/H<sub>2</sub> atmosphere at 700 °C for 3 h, the ZIF-67 precursors were converted into carbon polyhedra intertwined with a large number of surficial CNTs (Co@N-CF/CNTs). The growth of interconnected CNTs on the external surface of the carbon framework was attributed to the catalytic effect of Co nanoparticles under the reducing gas streams,[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0002_R_d17171647e600" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Small Chem. Eng. J. Adv. Energy Mater.">2</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0008_R_d17171647e600" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - J. Mater. Chem. A﻿﻿">8</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0009_R_d17171647e600" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Nano Lett. Nat. Energy">9</a></span>] which not only provided an interlaced conductive network to facilitate electrolyte penetration and charge transportation, but also effectively mitigated the volume expansion and maintained the structural integrity of the carbon matrix.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0002_R_d17171647e603" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Small Chem. Eng. J. Adv. Energy Mater.">2</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0008_R_d17171647e603" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - J. Mater. Chem. A﻿﻿">8</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0009_R_d17171647e603" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Nano Lett. Nat. Energy">9</a></span>] Figure <a href="#advs832-fig-0001">1</a>b,c shows the SEM and transmission electron microscopy (TEM) images of the CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs composite, which mostly reserved the original structural morphology of Co@N-CF/CNTs upon the selenization at 300 °C. The energy-dispersive X-ray spectra (EDX) of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs were shown in Figure S2 (Supporting Information). The uniform distribution of C, O, N, Co, and Se elements can be readily observed, and the atomic ratio of Se/Co (2.04) strongly supported the formation of CoSe<sub>2</sub>, which was well wrapped by the N-doped carbonaceous matrix. The encapsulation of CoSe<sub>2</sub> nanoparticles by carbon layers was further evidenced in high-resolution TEM (HRTEM) measurements (Figure <a href="#advs832-fig-0001">1</a>d). The interplanar spacing of 0.260 nm was in agreement with that of the (111) crystal plane of orthorhombic CoSe<sub>2</sub>.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="advs832-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/7d79a110-33f8-4978-9344-b7c3c0f454ba/advs832-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/7d79a110-33f8-4978-9344-b7c3c0f454ba/advs832-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/c55af678-d736-4538-8fa1-0c93db1a3a0f/advs832-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/7d79a110-33f8-4978-9344-b7c3c0f454ba/advs832-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=advs832-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadvs.201800763" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">SEM images of a) Co@N-CF/CNTs and b) CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs. c,d) TEM images of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The successful synthesis of ZIF-67 crystals is also confirmed in XRD measurements (Figure S3a, Supporting Information).<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0010_R_d17171647e644" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Science Small ACS Nano">10</a></span> Figure S3b (Supporting Information) shows the diffraction peaks of Co@N-CF/CNTs and Co@CF/CNTs derived from carbonization treatment of ZIF-67 at different temperatures, where the diffraction peaks for ZIF-67 crystal vanished completely, and three characteristic peaks for the (111), (200), and (220) lattice facets of metallic cobalt at 2θ = 44.22°, 51.52°, and 75.85° emerged, suggesting the formation of cobalt nanoparticles.<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0011_R_d17171647e646" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Electrochim. Acta Energy Environ. Sci.">11</a></span> These diffraction peaks of Co nanoparticles became increasingly intensified and sharpened with increasing calcination temperature, indicating enhanced crystallinity at elevated temperatures.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0005_R_d17171647e648" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Adv. Mater. Adv. Energy Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Coord. Chem. Rev.">5</a></span>] According to the Scherrer's equation, <i>d</i> = 0.89λ/βcosθ, where <i>d</i> presents the average size of the crystallites, λ is the X-ray wavelength, β is the full width at half-maximum (FWHM) for the Co(111) peak located at the diffraction angle θ, the average crystallite sizes were calculated to be 8.78 and 17.89 nm for Co@N-CF/CNTs and Co@CF/CNTs, respectively. The increment of calcination temperature resulted in larger sizes of Co crystallite. The tiny diffraction peak at 2θ = 26.38° was associated with the graphitic carbon, owing to the improved graphitic crystallinity during carbonization.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0011_R_d17171647e656" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Electrochim. Acta Energy Environ. Sci.">11</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0012_R_d17171647e656" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Nano Energy ACS Energy Lett.">12</a></span>] <b>Figure</b> <a href="#advs832-fig-0002">2</a>a shows the XRD patterns of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs and CoSe<sub>2</sub>@CF/CNTs prepared at an optimized temperature at 300 °C for 12 h, which are well indexed to orthorhombic CoSe<sub>2</sub> (PDF No. 53-0449; <i>Pnnm</i>(58), <i>a</i> = 3.643 Å, <i>b</i> = 4.896 Å, <i>c</i> = 5.821 Å). Co@N-CF/CNTs annealed with Se powder at elevated temperatures (400, 500, and 600 °C) displayed the reflections of CoSe at 2θ = 37.76° and 51.91° (PDF No. 09-0234; <i>Pa</i>3(205), <i>a</i> = 5.843 Å, <i>b</i> = 5.843 Å, <i>c</i> = 5.843 Å), as shown in Figure S4a (Supporting Information). Figure <a href="#advs832-fig-0002">2</a>b displays the Raman spectra of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs and CoSe<sub>2</sub>@CF/CNTs, where the two peaks at 672 and 188 cm<sup>−1</sup> are attributed to the A<sub>1g</sub> and A<sub>g</sub> modes of CoSe<sub>2</sub>,<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0008_R_d17171647e703" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - J. Mater. Chem. A﻿﻿">8</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0013_R_d17171647e703" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Electrochim. Acta">13</a></span> while the three minor bands at 469, 511, and 607 cm<sup>−1</sup> are possibly associated with the E<sub>g</sub>, <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/0d8f0ad7-8d8d-445c-9d48-8a7866933bfd/advs832-math-0001.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:advs832:advs832-math-0001" display="inline" location="graphic/advs832-math-0001.png">
                  <mrow>
                     <msubsup>
                        <mi mathvariant="normal">F</mi>
                        <mrow>
                           <mn>2</mn>
                           <mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi>
                        </mrow>
                        <mrow>
                           <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
                           <mn>2</mn>
                           <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
                        </mrow>
                     </msubsup>
                  </mrow></math>, and <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/b600dc18-2d73-4c84-88ee-5706fee9face/advs832-math-0002.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:advs832:advs832-math-0002" display="inline" location="graphic/advs832-math-0002.png">
                  <mrow>
                     <msubsup>
                        <mi mathvariant="normal">F</mi>
                        <mrow>
                           <mn>2</mn>
                           <mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi>
                        </mrow>
                        <mrow>
                           <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
                           <mn>1</mn>
                           <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
                        </mrow>
                     </msubsup>
                  </mrow></math> modes of Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> caused by slight surface oxidation.<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0008_R_d17171647e746" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - J. Mater. Chem. A﻿﻿">8</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0013_R_d17171647e746" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Electrochim. Acta">13</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0014_R_d17171647e746" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Solid State Commun.">14</a></span> The two peaks at 1346 and 1585 cm<sup>−1</sup> are due to the characteristic D and G bands of the carbon framework.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0009_R_d17171647e751" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Nano Lett. Nat. Energy">9</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0012_R_d17171647e751" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Nano Energy ACS Energy Lett.">12</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0015_R_d17171647e751" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - Nat. Chem.">15</a></span>] CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs exhibited a somewhat lower <i>I</i><sub>D</sub>/<i>I</i><sub>G</sub> ratio than CoSe<sub>2</sub>@CF/CNTs (0.98 vs 1.02), implying a higher degree of graphitization, which was favorable for improved electrical conductivity.<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0016_R_d17171647e765" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Energy Environ. Sci. ACS Nano">16</a></span></p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="advs832-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/4cc080bd-4b7c-4761-a90e-2c322eb01276/advs832-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/4cc080bd-4b7c-4761-a90e-2c322eb01276/advs832-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/33795c6d-9880-412e-b84c-bdda1d59e9ad/advs832-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/4cc080bd-4b7c-4761-a90e-2c322eb01276/advs832-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=advs832-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadvs.201800763" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) XRD patterns, b) Raman spectra, and c) TGA curves of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs and CoSe<sub>2</sub>@CF/CNTs.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The weight percentages of CoSe<sub>2</sub> in CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs and CoSe<sub>2</sub>@CF/CNTs composites were determined by thermogravimetric analysis (TGA) measurements in an O<sub>2</sub> atmosphere at a heating rate of 10 °C min<sup>−1</sup> from 30 to 800 °C, as shown in Figure <a href="#advs832-fig-0002">2</a>c. We can see that CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs exhibited one step of weight increase and multiple steps of weight loss. The small mass loss below 200 °C was attributed to the evaporation of adsorbed water. The slight weight increase between 200 and 350 °C was likely due to the oxidation of cobalt and selenium species, partially transforming CoSe<sub>2</sub> into CoSe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub>.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0003_R_d17171647e810" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - ACS Energy Lett. Chem. Eng. J.">3</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0005_R_d17171647e810" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Adv. Mater. Adv. Energy Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Coord. Chem. Rev.">5</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0017_R_d17171647e810" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Phys. B﻿﻿">17</a></span>] The major mass loss between 350 and 800 °C was ascribed to the oxidation of CoSe<sub>2</sub> to Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub>, the combustion of carbon, and transformation of CoSe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub> to Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub>.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0003_R_d17171647e829" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - ACS Energy Lett. Chem. Eng. J.">3</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0005_R_d17171647e829" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Adv. Mater. Adv. Energy Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Coord. Chem. Rev.">5</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0018_R_d17171647e829" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - ChemElectroChem">18</a></span>] On the basis of the final product Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> (XRD pattern in Figure S4b in the Supporting Information), the weight percentages of CoSe<sub>2</sub> in CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs and CoSe<sub>2</sub>@CF/CNTs were calculated to be 65.4 and 68.6 wt%, respectively. In addition, N<sub>2</sub> adsorption–desorption isotherms of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs and CoSe<sub>2</sub>@CF/CNTs were shown in Figure S5 (Supporting Information), which are characteristic of type IV isotherms with hysteresis loops at high relative pressures, indicating the formation of a mesoporous configuration.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0005_R_d17171647e849" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Adv. Mater. Adv. Energy Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Coord. Chem. Rev.">5</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0019_R_d17171647e849" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - Pure Appl. Chem.">19</a></span>] The specific surface areas of Co@N-CF/CNTs and Co@CF/CNTs derived from the isotherms were 277.59 and 237.96 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, with the pore size of 2–6 nm. The slightly smaller specific surface area of Co@CF/CNTs than Co@N-CF/CNTs was likely due to the aggregation of cobalt nanoparticles at higher temperatures.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0005_R_d17171647e857" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Adv. Mater. Adv. Energy Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Coord. Chem. Rev.">5</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0020_R_d17171647e857" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Small J. Am. Chem. Soc. Energy Environ. Sci.">20</a></span>] Selenization of Co@N-CF/CNTs and Co@CF/CNTs remarkably reduced the specific surface area and total pore volume of the composites (Table S1, Supporting Information) due to the formation of CoSe<sub>2</sub> nanoparticles. The CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNT sample has the largest average pore diameter of 31.39 nm and the submaximal total pore volume of 0.134 cm<sup>3</sup> g<sup>−1</sup>, which was favorable to facilitate access of the electrode surface by electrolyte and thus to accelerate ion diffusion, electron transfer, and electrolyte infiltration. Importantly, the porous structure may also effectively buffer the large volume expansion during repeated charge/discharge process, leading to enhanced Li<sup>+</sup>/Na<sup>+</sup> storage capacity and rate capability.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0003_R_d17171647e873" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - ACS Energy Lett. Chem. Eng. J.">3</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0005_R_d17171647e873" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Adv. Mater. Adv. Energy Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Coord. Chem. Rev.">5</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0021_R_d17171647e873" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - ACS Nano Adv. Energy Mater. J. Mater. Chem.">21</a></span>]</p>
            
            <p>The chemical compositions of Co@N-CF/CNTs and Co@CF/CNTs were then examined by X-ray photoelectron spectra (XPS) measurements. The full survey spectra in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#advs832-fig-0003">3</a>a indicate the presence of Co, C, O, and N elements in Co@N-CF/CNTs, whereas only trace amount of N can be identified for Co@CF/CNTs. By quantitative XPS analysis, the atomic percentages of N element in Co@N-CF/CNTs and Co@CF/CNTs are 7.53% and 1.01% (Table S2, Supporting Information), respectively. The high-resolution N 1s scan of Co@N-CF/CNTs is displayed in Figure <a href="#advs832-fig-0003">3</a>b and can be deconvoluted into five subpeaks. The three main peaks at 398.19, 399.02, and 400.74 eV are attributed to pyridinic N, pyrrolic N, graphitic N, respectively,[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0005_R_d17171647e886" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Adv. Mater. Adv. Energy Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Coord. Chem. Rev.">5</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0011_R_d17171647e886" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Electrochim. Acta Energy Environ. Sci.">11</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0020_R_d17171647e886" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Small J. Am. Chem. Soc. Energy Environ. Sci.">20</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0022_R_d17171647e886" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Nat. Commun. J. Mater. Chem. A﻿﻿">22</a></span>] whereas the small pair at the binding energy of 402.11 and 402.75 eV is assigned to oxidized N.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0005_R_d17171647e889" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Adv. Mater. Adv. Energy Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Coord. Chem. Rev.">5</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0020_R_d17171647e889" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Small J. Am. Chem. Soc. Energy Environ. Sci.">20</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0023_R_d17171647e889" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - Adv. Funct. Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Carbon Carbon">23</a></span>] The schematic bonding structure of the four types of N dopants is shown in Figure <a href="#advs832-fig-0003">3</a>g. The C 1s spectrum is shown in Figure <a href="#advs832-fig-0003">3</a>c, and can be deconvoluted into three peaks at 284.6, 285.46, and 287.5 eV, which are attributed to graphitic sp<sup>2</sup> C,[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0011_R_d17171647e899" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Electrochim. Acta Energy Environ. Sci.">11</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0020_R_d17171647e899" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Small J. Am. Chem. Soc. Energy Environ. Sci.">20</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0024_R_d17171647e899" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Chem. Mater. J. Phys. Chem. C﻿﻿ Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">24</a></span>] N<span class="icomoon"></span>sp<sup>2</sup> C, and N<span class="icomoon"></span>sp<sup>3</sup> C species,[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0005_R_d17171647e907" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Adv. Mater. Adv. Energy Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Coord. Chem. Rev.">5</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0011_R_d17171647e907" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Electrochim. Acta Energy Environ. Sci.">11</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0025_R_d17171647e907" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - ACS Nano Adv. Mater. Nano Lett.">25</a></span>] respectively, further confirming the incorporation of N atoms into the carbon matrix. In contrast, no signal of N 1s (Figure <a href="#advs832-fig-0003">3</a>b) was detected in Co@CF/CNTs, possibly due to the escape of nitrogen at higher annealing temperatures.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0011_R_d17171647e912" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Electrochim. Acta Energy Environ. Sci.">11</a></span>] The peak at 285.57 eV for Co@CF/CNTs (Figure S6a, Supporting Information) was ascribed to the formation of C<span class="icomoon"></span>O bond during the annealing process.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0023_R_d17171647e915" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - Adv. Funct. Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Carbon Carbon">23</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0024_R_d17171647e915" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Chem. Mater. J. Phys. Chem. C﻿﻿ Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">24</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0026_R_d17171647e915" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Nanoscale">26</a></span>]</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="advs832-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/92bcfd56-b464-4361-accf-5952d5cd1439/advs832-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/92bcfd56-b464-4361-accf-5952d5cd1439/advs832-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/6ecb4005-825b-4fd3-8efa-9bfbe2d4dc31/advs832-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/92bcfd56-b464-4361-accf-5952d5cd1439/advs832-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=advs832-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadvs.201800763" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Survey XPS and b) high-resolution N 1s spectra of Co@CF/CNTs (top) and Co@N-CF/CNTs (bottom). c) High-resolution C 1s spectrum of Co@N-CF/CNTs. d) Survey XPS and e) high-resolution Co 2p spectra of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs and CoSe<sub>2</sub>@CF/CNTs. f) High-resolution Se 3d spectrum of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs. g) Schematic representation of the N configuration in carbon matrix.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The full survey XPS of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs and CoSe<sub>2</sub>@CF/CNTs were shown in Figure <a href="#advs832-fig-0003">3</a>d, where C, O, Co, and Se were clearly observed. As illustrated in Figure <a href="#advs832-fig-0003">3</a>e, the binding energies of Co 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and Co 2p<sub>1/2</sub> for CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs were identified at 778.5 and 793.3 eV, respectively, in accord with those of CoSe<sub>2</sub>.<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0027_R_d17171647e959" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - J. Am. Chem. Soc. Chem. Mater. J. Solid State Chem.">27</a></span> However, the binding energies of Co 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and Co 2p<sub>1/2</sub> for CoSe<sub>2</sub>@CF/CNT composite were observed at 780.9 and at 796.0 eV, implying the existence of oxidic Co,[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0005_R_d17171647e968" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Adv. Mater. Adv. Energy Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Coord. Chem. Rev.">5</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0028_R_d17171647e968" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. J. Alloys Compd. Nanotechnology">28</a></span>] which might be ascribed to the partial surface oxidation of Co when exposed to air. On the other hand, the electron clouds have not been biased from CF to CoSe<sub>2</sub> for CoSe<sub>2</sub>@CF/CNTs after Se incorporation owing to the absence of nitrogen dopant in carbon host.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0016_R_d17171647e975" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Energy Environ. Sci. ACS Nano">16</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0029_R_d17171647e975" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Nano Lett. Science Adv. Energy Mater.">29</a></span>] This perspective can be further proved by the much more intense peak of Se 3d electrons of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@CF/CNTs (Figure S6b, Supporting Information) at 59.2 eV than CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs (Figure <a href="#advs832-fig-0003">3</a>f) at 59.4 eV, which mainly originated from the intense interaction between Se and O atoms in the carbon matrix. In Figure <a href="#advs832-fig-0003">3</a>f, the two peaks at 54.8 and 55.5 eV are assigned to Se 3d<sub>5/2</sub> and 3d<sub>3/2</sub> of CoSe<sub>2</sub> of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0011_R_d17171647e996" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Electrochim. Acta Energy Environ. Sci.">11</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0027_R_d17171647e996" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - J. Am. Chem. Soc. Chem. Mater. J. Solid State Chem.">27</a></span>]</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="advs832-sec-0040">
            
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="advs832-sec-0040-title">2.2 Electrochemical Characterization</h3>
            
            <p>The electrochemical properties of the CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs composite as an anode material for LIBs were then evaluated by using a 2032-type coin cell assembled with a metallic lithium foil as the counter and reference electrode. The three initial cyclic voltammetry (CV) scans for CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs were measured between 0.5 and 3.0 V at the scan rate of 0.2 mV s<sup>−1</sup>, as shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#advs832-fig-0004">4</a>a. The first CV curve displayed a much different shape from those of the following cycles. Specifically, the cathodic peaks at 1.59 and 1.39 V can be ascribed to the lithium insertion, corresponding to the sequential conversion of CoSe<sub>2</sub> to Li<i><sub>x</sub></i>CoSe<sub>2</sub>,[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0005_R_d17171647e1030" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Adv. Mater. Adv. Energy Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Coord. Chem. Rev.">5</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0030_R_d17171647e1030" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Nano Energy Chem. - Eur. J. Small ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces J. Power Sources Adv. Mater. J. Power Sources">30</a></span>] and then to metallic Co and Li<sub>2</sub>Se.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0018_R_d17171647e1035" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - ChemElectroChem">18</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0030_R_d17171647e1035" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Nano Energy Chem. - Eur. J. Small ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces J. Power Sources Adv. Mater. J. Power Sources">30</a></span>] Besides, the appearance of a weak and broad peak around 0.65 V is indicative of the inevitable formation of a solid electrolyte interface (SEI) film caused by the electrolyte decomposition and reaction on the anode surface.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0005_R_d17171647e1039" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Adv. Mater. Adv. Energy Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Coord. Chem. Rev.">5</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0018_R_d17171647e1039" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - ChemElectroChem">18</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0030_R_d17171647e1039" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Nano Energy Chem. - Eur. J. Small ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces J. Power Sources Adv. Mater. J. Power Sources">30</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0031_R_d17171647e1039" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - J. Phys. Chem. Lett.">31</a></span>] In the anodic scan, two oxidation peaks at 2.11 and 2.27 V corresponded to the sequential phase transitions of the delithiation process.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0018_R_d17171647e1042" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - ChemElectroChem">18</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0030_R_d17171647e1042" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Nano Energy Chem. - Eur. J. Small ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces J. Power Sources Adv. Mater. J. Power Sources">30</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0032_R_d17171647e1042" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces J. Phys. Chem. C﻿﻿">32</a></span>] In the following CV scans, the cathodic peaks shifted toward the positive voltages, from 1.59 and 1.39 to 1.77 and 1.43 V, respectively, which probably originated from the electrochemical activation of the electrode materials in the 1st cycle.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0005_R_d17171647e1045" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Adv. Mater. Adv. Energy Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Coord. Chem. Rev.">5</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0018_R_d17171647e1045" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - ChemElectroChem">18</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0030_R_d17171647e1045" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Nano Energy Chem. - Eur. J. Small ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces J. Power Sources Adv. Mater. J. Power Sources">30</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0033_R_d17171647e1045" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - ACS Nano">33</a></span>] Additionally, the second and third CV scans of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs are much better overlapped, as compared with CoSe<sub>2</sub>@CF/CNTs and other samples (Figure S7, Supporting Information), suggesting much more stable cycling performance of the former than the latter.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="advs832-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/4d9dcdad-2128-47c6-a888-ceb600f5d665/advs832-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/4d9dcdad-2128-47c6-a888-ceb600f5d665/advs832-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/17c42f3c-07b7-446d-ab5f-efbf7ee472d0/advs832-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/4d9dcdad-2128-47c6-a888-ceb600f5d665/advs832-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=advs832-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadvs.201800763" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) CV curves of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs at a scan rate of 0.2 mV s<sup>−1</sup> in the voltage range of 3.0–0.5 V versus Li/Li<sup>+</sup>. b) Galvanostatic discharge and charge curves of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs at a current rate of 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>. c) Comparison of cycling performance of as-prepared electrodes at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>. d) Cycle life comparison of anode materials for LIBs in this work and previous literatures. e) Rate capability of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs at increasing current density from 0.2 to 10 A g<sup>−1</sup>. f) The corresponding charge/discharge profiles at various rates.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The galvanostatic discharge and charge profiles of the CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs composite from 0.5 to 3.0 V at the current rate of 1 A g<sup>−1</sup> are displayed in Figure <a href="#advs832-fig-0004">4</a>b, and from the 1st cycle, the discharge and charge capacities were estimated to be 687 and 562 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, with an initial Coulombic efficiency of 81.88%. Figure <a href="#advs832-fig-0004">4</a>c shows the cycling performance of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs, CoSe<sub>2</sub>@CF/CNTs, and other samples at a current density of 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>. CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs can be seen to deliver a reversible capacity of 428 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 500 cycles with the Coulombic efficiency of almost 100%, corresponding to a high capacity retention of 92.58% and extremely slow capacity decay rate of 0.016% per cycle calculated from the 30th cycle. The enhanced cycling stability of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs, as compared to that of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@CF/CNTs, is probably due to the improved binding strength between CoSe<sub>2</sub> and the N-doped carbon matrix.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0011_R_d17171647e1115" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Electrochim. Acta Energy Environ. Sci.">11</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0016_R_d17171647e1115" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Energy Environ. Sci. ACS Nano">16</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0034_R_d17171647e1115" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Chem. Mater.">34</a></span>] It is noted that the average crystal size of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs, with dwelling time of 12 h during selenization of Co@N-CF/CNTs, is much bigger than those of other samples (Figure S8 and Table S3, Supporting Information), which might be equally responsible for the improved cycling performance of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs. The gravimetric capacity and cycling performance of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs and other anode materials for LIBs in recent literatures are summarized in Table S4 (Supporting Information) and compared in Figure <a href="#advs832-fig-0004">4</a>d. It can be seen that the cycle stability of the CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs electrodes is markedly better than that of other typical transition metal chalcogenide anodes, especially in the long charge/discharge process. The rate performance of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs is depicted in Figure <a href="#advs832-fig-0004">4</a>e, with the specific capacity of 666, 580, 531, 487, 439, and 406 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at the current rate of 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5, and 10 A g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. Furthermore, when the current rate was reversed back to 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup>, the composite recovered most of its specific capacity and reached a value of 534 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>. The capacity fading, compared to that of the initial few cycles, is probably due to the activation process similar to its cyclic behavior. To minimize the impact of the initial decay and evaluate the intrinsic rate performance of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs, the rate capability was further tested after first 30 cycles of activation at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure S9, Supporting Information). It can be seen that the capacity was almost completely recovered to the initial value when the current rate was reduced to 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup>. Figure <a href="#advs832-fig-0004">4</a>f depicts the corresponding charge/discharge voltage curves at the current density of 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5, and 10 A g<sup>−1</sup> of the CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs electrode in the potential range of 0.5–3.0 V. Interestingly, even though the voltage gap was gradually enlarged with increasing current density, the voltage plateaus contributing to the charge and discharge capacities remain be obviously defined for all charge/discharge profiles, owing to the increasing polarization loss and mechanical energy dissipation, which indicates outstanding rate capability of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0001_R_d17171647e1157" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Chem. Rev. Chem. Soc. Rev. Adv. Funct. Mater. ACS Nano Nano Energy">1</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0005_R_d17171647e1157" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Adv. Mater. Adv. Energy Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Coord. Chem. Rev.">5</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0035_R_d17171647e1157" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - J. Mater. Chem. A﻿﻿">35</a></span>] As an optimizing process, the electrochemical performance of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs electrodes with ether-based electrolyte and polyvinylidene fluoride (PVDF) binder were studied and shown in Figure S10 (Supporting Information). The inferior performance of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs electrodes here was attributed to the dissolution of the intermediate products into the ether-based electrolyte<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0036_R_d17171647e1165" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - J. Am. Chem. Soc. ACS Nano">36</a></span> and the lack of strong adhesion between the electrode layer and copper foil,<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0037_R_d17171647e1167" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Science">37</a></span> respectively.</p>
            
            <p>The mechanism for lithium-ion storage was then investigated by means of ex situ XRD measurements. As shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#advs832-fig-0005">5</a>, the XRD patterns of CoSe<sub>2</sub> continuously descended and shifted toward lower 2θ values when the cells was discharged to 1.75 and 1.55 V, which might be attributed to the intercalation of Li ions within the host CoSe<sub>2</sub> materials, the formation of Li<i><sub>x</sub></i>CoSe<sub>2</sub> intermediates, and the expansion of interlayer spacing, as observed previously for the intercalation of Li and Na ions into NiSe<sub>2</sub>, MoS<sub>2</sub>, and FeS<sub>2</sub>.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0030_R_d17171647e1193" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Nano Energy Chem. - Eur. J. Small ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces J. Power Sources Adv. Mater. J. Power Sources">30</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0038_R_d17171647e1193" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Nat. Nanotechnol. Adv. Funct. Mater.">38</a></span>] When further discharged to 1.4, 0.9, and 0.5 V, the diffraction peaks of CoSe<sub>2</sub> vanished and the diffraction peaks of Li<sub>2</sub>Se (111) and (200) lattice facets emerged at 2θ = 25.68° and 29.74° (PDF no. 23-0072). The evolution of the XRD patterns during discharging process suggested the conversion of CoSe<sub>2</sub> to Li<i><sub>x</sub></i>CoSe<sub>2</sub> and further to Li<sub>2</sub>Se and Co. In the continuous charging process, the diffractions peaks of Li<sub>2</sub>Se can be clearly observed when charged back to 1.8 and 2.0 V, but completely disappeared when further charged to 2.5 and 3.0 V. This suggests that the conversion reactions happened between 2.0 and 2.5 V. Although CoSe<sub>2</sub> failed to be detected in XRD measurements even if the electrode was fully charged to 3.0 V, ex situ Raman analysis clearly confirmed the A<sub>g</sub> vibrational mode of CoSe<sub>2</sub> at the fully charged state of 3.0 V in the 1st cycle (Figure S11, Supporting Information). The absence of CoSe<sub>2</sub> in XRD measurements during the charging process might be attributed to the poor crystallinity of the electrochemically regenerated CoSe<sub>2</sub>,[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0001_R_d17171647e1223" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Chem. Rev. Chem. Soc. Rev. Adv. Funct. Mater. ACS Nano Nano Energy">1</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0003_R_d17171647e1223" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - ACS Energy Lett. Chem. Eng. J.">3</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0005_R_d17171647e1223" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Adv. Mater. Adv. Energy Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Coord. Chem. Rev.">5</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0038_R_d17171647e1223" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Nat. Nanotechnol. Adv. Funct. Mater.">38</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0039_R_d17171647e1223" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Small J. Mater. Chem. A﻿﻿">39</a></span>] as well as the interference of conductive additive, binder, and copper current collector.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0001_R_d17171647e1227" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Chem. Rev. Chem. Soc. Rev. Adv. Funct. Mater. ACS Nano Nano Energy">1</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0040_R_d17171647e1227" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Adv. Mater.">40</a></span>] To recap, the structural evolution of the as-prepared CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs at different charge and discharge states is well consistent with the voltage curve and CV result. Based on the facts established above and from relevant literatures, the reaction mechanism of this composite can be described as follows:</p>

               <figure class="figure" id="advs832-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/26e9e7a0-92aa-4405-9fba-6b1349e7e2fc/advs832-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>

                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) XRD patterns of the CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs electrodes obtained at various charge–discharge states for the 1st cycle. b) The corresponding charge–discharge curve.</div>

               </figure>
            </section>
            <div class="paragraph-element">In the discharge process

            <div class="paragraph-element">In the charge process

            <div class="paragraph-element">Total reaction equation
               <div class="inline-equation" id="advs832-disp-0005"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE--><span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/63c5630b-2f8b-425a-8072-b8642a0d4a3c/advs832-math-0007.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:advs832:advs832-math-0007" display="block" location="graphic/advs832-math-0007.png">

            <p>Galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) was employed to evaluate ion insertion and extraction levels and the electrochemical reaction kinetics of the as-prepared electrodes. <b>Figure</b> <a href="#advs832-fig-0006">6</a>a,b plotted the potential response curves of CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs and CoSe<sub>2</sub>@CF/CNTs for both lithiation and delithiation processes during the 1st cycle, in which the overpotential looks stable and remains at a very low level. Furthermore, the CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs electrode exhibited slightly lower reaction resistances for both Li<sup>+</sup> insertion and extraction processes than CoSe<sub>2</sub>@CF/CNTs, indicating the improved lithium-ion diffusion kinetics and explaining well the superior electrochemical performance of the CoSe<sub>2</sub>@N-CF/CNTs composite.[<span><a href="#advs832-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0023_R_d17171647e1448" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - Adv. Funct. Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Carbon Carbon">23</a>, <a href="#advs832-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs832-bib-0041_R_d17171647e1448" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Adv. Energy Mater. Adv. Energy Mater. Korean J. Chem. Eng.">41</a></span>]</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="advs832-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/cf8c7504-8db3-457a-af1d-6cf6ebe0a65e/advs832-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/cf8c7504-8db3-457a-af1d-6cf6ebe0a65e/advs832-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/61ffc2c5-f54f-4924-8e79-8a948fe95efe/advs832-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/cf8c7504-8db3-457a-af1d-6cf6ebe0a65e/advs832-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=advs832-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadvs.201800763" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
